<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en"><i>Harry Potter</i> (film series)</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><i><b>Harry Potter</b></i> is a British-American <a href="/wiki/Film_series" title="Film series">film series</a> based on the <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter" title="Harry Potter">Harry Potter</a></i> novels by author <a href="/wiki/J._K._Rowling" title="J. K. Rowling">J. K. Rowling</a>. The series is distributed by <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> and consists of eight <a href="/wiki/Fantasy_film" title="Fantasy film">fantasy films</a>, beginning with <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Philosopher&#39;s Stone (film)">Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone</a></i> (2001) and culminating with <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2</a></i> (2011).<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Spin-off_(media)" title="Spin-off (media)">spin-off</a> <a href="/wiki/Prequel" title="Prequel">prequel</a> series will consist of five films, starting with <i><a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Beasts_and_Where_to_Find_Them_(film)" title="Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them (film)">Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them</a></i> (2016), marking the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Wizarding_World" title="Wizarding World">Wizarding World</a> shared media franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The series was mainly produced by <a href="/wiki/David_Heyman" title="David Heyman">David Heyman</a>, and stars <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Radcliffe" title="Daniel Radcliffe">Daniel Radcliffe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Grint" title="Rupert Grint">Rupert Grint</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Emma_Watson" title="Emma Watson">Emma Watson</a> as the three leading characters: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(character)" title="Harry Potter (character)">Harry Potter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Weasley" title="Ron Weasley">Ron Weasley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hermione_Granger" title="Hermione Granger">Hermione Granger</a>. Four directors worked on the series: <a href="/wiki/Chris_Columbus_(filmmaker)" title="Chris Columbus (filmmaker)">Chris Columbus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso Cuarón">Alfonso Cuarón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Newell_(director)" title="Mike Newell (director)">Mike Newell</a>, and <a href="/wiki/David_Yates" title="David Yates">David Yates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Four_Directors_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Four_Directors-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Goldenberg" title="Michael Goldenberg">Michael Goldenberg</a> wrote the screenplay for <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix (film)">Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</a></i> (2007), while the remaining films had their screenplays written by <a href="/wiki/Steve_Kloves" title="Steve Kloves">Steve Kloves</a>. Production took place over ten years, with the main <a href="/wiki/Story_arc" title="Story arc">story arc</a> following Harry Potter's quest to overcome his arch-enemy <a href="/wiki/Lord_Voldemort" title="Lord Voldemort">Lord Voldemort</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WarnerBrosStudioInfo_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WarnerBrosStudioInfo-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</a></i>, the seventh and final novel in the series, was adapted into two feature-length parts.<sup id="cite_ref-BusinessWireDeathlyHallows_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BusinessWireDeathlyHallows-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_1" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 1">Part 1</a></i> was released in November 2010, and <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2">Part 2</a></i> was released in July 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Bocher_&amp;_Eller_(2010-11-07)_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bocher_&amp;_Eller_(2010-11-07)-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schuker_(2010-11-22)_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schuker_(2010-11-22)-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Five of the series' eight films are among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">50 highest-grossing films of all time</a>, with <i>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2</i> the highest-grossing film in the series and one of 36 films to gross over $1 billion, ranking at number ten. Without inflation adjustment, it is <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_film_series#Highest-grossing_franchises_and_film_series" class="mw-redirect" title="List of highest-grossing film series">the third highest-grossing film series</a> with $7.7 billion in worldwide receipts.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span></h2>
<p>Late in 1997, film producer David Heyman's London offices received a copy of the first book in what would become Rowling's series of seven <i>Harry Potter</i> novels. The book, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone" title="Harry Potter and the Philosopher&#39;s Stone">Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone</a></i>, was relegated to a low-priority bookshelf, where it was discovered by a secretary who read it and gave it to Heyman with a positive review. Consequently, Heyman, who had originally disliked "the rubbish title", read the book himself. Highly impressed by Rowling's work, he began the process that led to one of the most successful cinematic franchises of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-latimesblogs.latimes.com_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimesblogs.latimes.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Heyman's enthusiasm led to Rowling's 1999 sale of the film rights for the first four <i>Harry Potter</i> books to Warner Bros. for a reported <a href="/wiki/British_pound" class="mw-redirect" title="British pound">£</a>1 million (US$2,000,000).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> A demand Rowling made was that the principal cast be kept strictly British, allowing nevertheless for the inclusion of many Irish actors, such as <a href="/wiki/Richard_Harris" title="Richard Harris">Richard Harris</a> as Dumbledore, and for casting of French and Eastern European actors in <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire">Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</a></i> where characters from the book are specified as such.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Rowling was hesitant to sell the rights because she "didn't want to give them control over the rest of the story" by selling the rights to the characters, which would have enabled Warner Bros. to make non-author-written sequels.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> initially negotiated to direct the first film, he declined the offer.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Spielberg wanted the adaptation to be an <a href="/wiki/Animated_film" class="mw-redirect" title="Animated film">animated film</a>, with American actor <a href="/wiki/Haley_Joel_Osment" title="Haley Joel Osment">Haley Joel Osment</a> providing Harry Potter's voice.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2018)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Spielberg contended that, in his opinion, there was every expectation of profit in making the film. He claims that making money would have been like "shooting ducks in a barrel. It's just a slam dunk. It's just like withdrawing a billion dollars and putting it into your personal bank accounts. There's no challenge".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In the "Rubbish" Bin section of her website, Rowling maintains that she had no role in choosing directors for the films, writing "Anyone who thinks I could (or would) have 'veto-ed' him [Spielberg] needs their <a href="/wiki/Quick-Quotes_Quill" class="mw-redirect" title="Quick-Quotes Quill">Quick-Quotes Quill</a> serviced."<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Spielberg left, conversations began with other directors, including <a href="/wiki/Chris_Columbus_(filmmaker)" title="Chris Columbus (filmmaker)">Chris Columbus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Demme" title="Jonathan Demme">Jonathan Demme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terry_Gilliam#Gilliam_and_Harry_Potter" title="Terry Gilliam">Terry Gilliam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Newell_(director)" title="Mike Newell (director)">Mike Newell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Parker" title="Alan Parker">Alan Parker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Petersen" title="Wolfgang Petersen">Wolfgang Petersen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rob_Reiner" title="Rob Reiner">Rob Reiner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Robbins" title="Tim Robbins">Tim Robbins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brad_Silberling" title="Brad Silberling">Brad Silberling</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Weir" title="Peter Weir">Peter Weir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Petersen and Reiner both pulled out of the running in March 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> It was then narrowed down to Columbus, Gilliam, Parker, and Silberling.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Rowling's first choice was Terry Gilliam.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> However, on 28 March 2000 Columbus was appointed as director of the film, with Warner Bros. citing his work on other family films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Home_Alone" title="Home Alone">Home Alone</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Mrs._Doubtfire" title="Mrs. Doubtfire">Mrs. Doubtfire</a></i> as influences for their decision.<sup id="cite_ref-columbus_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-columbus-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p><i>Harry Potter</i> is the kind of timeless literary achievement that comes around once in a lifetime. Since the books have generated such a passionate following across the world, it was important to us to find a director that has an affinity for both children and magic. I can't think of anyone more ideally suited for this job than Chris [Columbus].</p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8201;<cite><a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_di_Bonaventura" title="Lorenzo di Bonaventura">Lorenzo di Bonaventura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a><sup id="cite_ref-columbus_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-columbus-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Steve_Kloves" title="Steve Kloves">Steve Kloves</a> was selected to write the screenplay for the first film. He described adapting the book as "tough" since it did not "lend itself to adaptation as well as the next two books". Kloves was sent a "raft" of synopses of books proposed as film adaptations, with <i>Harry Potter</i> being the only one that jumped out at him. He went out and bought the book, becoming an instant fan. When speaking to Warner Bros. he stated that the film had to be British and true to the characters.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> David Heyman was confirmed to produce the film.<sup id="cite_ref-columbus_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-columbus-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Rowling received a large amount of creative control for the film, an arrangement that Columbus did not mind.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Warner Bros. had initially planned to release the first film over the 4 July 2001 weekend, making for such a short production window that several of the originally proposed directors had withdrawn themselves from contention. Eventually, due to time constraints, the date was put back to 16 November 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Casting_the_roles_of_Harry.2C_Ron.2C_and_Hermione"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Casting_the_roles_of_Harry,_Ron,_and_Hermione">Casting the roles of Harry, Ron, and Hermione</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Daniel_Radcliffe,_Emma_Watson_%26_Rupert_Grint_colour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Daniel_Radcliffe%2C_Emma_Watson_%26_Rupert_Grint_colour.jpg/220px-Daniel_Radcliffe%2C_Emma_Watson_%26_Rupert_Grint_colour.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Daniel_Radcliffe%2C_Emma_Watson_%26_Rupert_Grint_colour.jpg/330px-Daniel_Radcliffe%2C_Emma_Watson_%26_Rupert_Grint_colour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Daniel_Radcliffe%2C_Emma_Watson_%26_Rupert_Grint_colour.jpg/440px-Daniel_Radcliffe%2C_Emma_Watson_%26_Rupert_Grint_colour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="806" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Daniel_Radcliffe,_Emma_Watson_%26_Rupert_Grint_colour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Daniel_Radcliffe" title="Daniel Radcliffe">Daniel Radcliffe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emma_Watson" title="Emma Watson">Emma Watson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Grint" title="Rupert Grint">Rupert Grint</a> at the world premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Trafalgar_Square" title="Trafalgar Square">Trafalgar Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> on 7 July 2011</div></div></div>
<p>In 2000, after a seven-month search, lead actor <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Radcliffe" title="Daniel Radcliffe">Daniel Radcliffe</a> was discovered by producer David Heyman and writer Steve Kloves seated just behind them in a theatre. In Heyman's own words, "There sitting behind me was this boy with these big blue eyes. It was Dan Radcliffe. I remember my first impressions: He was curious and funny and so energetic. There was real generosity too, and sweetness. But at the same time he was really voracious and with hunger for knowledge of whatever kind."<sup id="cite_ref-latimesblogs.latimes.com_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimesblogs.latimes.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Radcliffe had already established himself as an actor in the 1999 <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> television production of <i><a href="/wiki/David_Copperfield_(novel)" class="mw-redirect" title="David Copperfield (novel)">David Copperfield</a></i> in which he played the title role's childhood years. Heyman persuaded Radcliffe's parents to allow him to audition for the part of <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(character)" title="Harry Potter (character)">Harry Potter</a>, which involved Radcliffe being filmed.<sup id="cite_ref-latimesblogs.latimes.com_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimesblogs.latimes.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> (This <a href="/wiki/Screen_test" title="Screen test">screen test</a> footage was released via the first set of Ultimate Editions in 2009.)<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Rowling was enthusiastic after viewing Radcliffe's filmed test, saying she didn't think there was a better choice for the part of Harry Potter.<sup id="cite_ref-latimesblogs.latimes.com_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimesblogs.latimes.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-news_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Also in 2000, the then unknown British actors <a href="/wiki/Emma_Watson" title="Emma Watson">Emma Watson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Grint" title="Rupert Grint">Rupert Grint</a> were selected from thousands of auditioning children to play the roles of <a href="/wiki/Hermione_Granger" title="Hermione Granger">Hermione Granger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ron_Weasley" title="Ron Weasley">Ron Weasley</a>, respectively. Their only previous acting experience was in school plays. Grint was eleven years old and Watson ten at the time they were cast.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> writer Geoff Boucher, who conducted the above-mentioned interview with Heyman, added that the casting of the three major roles "is especially impressive in hindsight. The trio's selection was arguably one of the best show-business decisions over the past decade... they have shown admirable grace and steadiness in the face of teen superstardom."<sup id="cite_ref-latimesblogs.latimes.com_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimesblogs.latimes.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-news_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span></h2>
<p>Filming of the series began at <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Studios,_Leavesden" title="Warner Bros. Studios, Leavesden">Leavesden Studios</a>, Hertfordshire, England, in September 2000 and ended in December 2010, with post-production on the final film lasting until summer 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-WarnerBrosStudioInfo_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WarnerBrosStudioInfo-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Leavesden Studios was the main base for filming <i>Harry Potter</i>, and it opened to the public as a studio tour in 2012 (renamed as Warner Bros. Studios, Leavesden).<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
