<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harry_Potter_Leavesden_entrance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Harry_Potter_Leavesden_entrance.jpg/220px-Harry_Potter_Leavesden_entrance.jpg" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Harry_Potter_Leavesden_entrance.jpg/330px-Harry_Potter_Leavesden_entrance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Harry_Potter_Leavesden_entrance.jpg/440px-Harry_Potter_Leavesden_entrance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harry_Potter_Leavesden_entrance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Studios,_Leavesden" title="Warner Bros. Studios, Leavesden">Warner Bros. Studios, Leavesden</a>, where much of the film series was shot. <i>Harry Potter</i> was also filmed in other areas, including <a href="/wiki/Pinewood_Studios" title="Pinewood Studios">Pinewood Studios</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>David Heyman produced all the films in the series with his production company <a href="/wiki/Heyday_Films" title="Heyday Films">Heyday Films</a>, while David Barron joined the series as an executive producer on <i>Chamber of Secrets</i> and <i>Goblet of Fire</i>. Barron was later appointed producer on the last four films. Chris Columbus was an executive producer on the first two films alongside <a href="/wiki/Mark_Radcliffe_(film_producer)" title="Mark Radcliffe (film producer)">Mark Radcliffe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Barnathan" title="Michael Barnathan">Michael Barnathan</a>, but he became a producer on the third film alongside Heyman and Radcliffe. Other executive producers include <a href="/wiki/Tanya_Seghatchian" title="Tanya Seghatchian">Tanya Seghatchian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Wigram_(cinema)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lionel Wigram (cinema)">Lionel Wigram</a>. J. K. Rowling, author of the series, was asked to become a producer on <i>Goblet of Fire</i> but declined. She subsequently accepted the role on the two-part <i>Deathly Hallows</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Heyday Films and Columbus' company <a href="/wiki/1492_Pictures" title="1492 Pictures">1492 Pictures</a> collaborated with Duncan Henderson Productions in 2001, Miracle Productions in 2002, and P of A Productions in 2004. Even though <i>Prisoner of Azkaban</i> was the final film produced by 1492 Pictures, Heyday Films continued with the franchise and collaborated with Patalex IV Productions in 2005. The sixth film in the series, <i>Half-Blood Prince</i>, was the most expensive film to produce as of  2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Harry_Potter_(film_series)&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> split the seventh and final novel in the series, <i>Deathly Hallows</i>, into two cinematic parts. The two parts were filmed back-to-back from early 2009 to summer 2010, with the completion of reshoots taking place on 21 December 2010; this marked the end of filming <i>Harry Potter</i>. Heyman stated that <i>Deathly Hallows</i> was "<a href="/wiki/Production_of_Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" title="Production of Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows">shot as one film</a>" but released in two feature-length parts.<sup id="cite_ref-empireheyman_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-empireheyman-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Tim Burke, the visual effects supervisor of the series, said of the production on <i>Harry Potter</i>, "It was this huge family; I think there were over 700 people working at Leavesden, an industry in itself." David Heyman said, "When the first film opened, no way did I think we'd make eight films. That didn't seem feasible until after we'd done the fourth." Nisha Parti, the production consultant on the first film, said that Heyman "made the first film very much the way he felt the studio Warner Bros. wanted to make it." After the film's success, Heyman was given "more freedom".<sup id="cite_ref-10YearsHP_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10YearsHP-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One of the aims of the filmmakers from the beginning of production was to develop the maturity of the films. Chris Columbus stated, "We realised that these movies would get progressively darker. Again, we didn't know <i>how</i> dark but we realised that as the kids get older, the movies get a little edgier and darker."<sup id="cite_ref-ColumbusDark_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ColumbusDark-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> This transpired with the succeeding three directors who would work on the series in the following years, with the films beginning to deal with issues such as death, betrayal, prejudice, and political corruption as the series developed narratively and thematically.<sup id="cite_ref-Four_Directors_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Four_Directors-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Directors">Directors</span></h3>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Chris_Columbus_(filmmaker)" title="Chris Columbus (filmmaker)">Chris Columbus</a> had finished working on <i>Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone</i>, he was hired to direct the second film, <i>Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</i>. The production started within a week after the release of the first film. Columbus was set to direct all entries in the series,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> but he did not want to return for the third film, <i>Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</i>, claiming he was "burned out".<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> He moved to the position of producer, while <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso Cuarón">Alfonso Cuarón</a> was approached for the role of director. He was initially nervous about directing the instalment since he had not read any of the books or seen the films. After reading the series, he changed his mind and signed on to direct since he had immediately connected to the story.<sup id="cite_ref-cuaroninternewsround_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cuaroninternewsround-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Yates_(27996598333).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/David_Yates_%2827996598333%29.jpg/220px-David_Yates_%2827996598333%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/David_Yates_%2827996598333%29.jpg/330px-David_Yates_%2827996598333%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/David_Yates_%2827996598333%29.jpg/440px-David_Yates_%2827996598333%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:David_Yates_(27996598333).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/David_Yates" title="David Yates">David Yates</a> directed four of the films in the series, including the two-part finale <i>Deathly Hallows</i>.</div></div></div>
<p>Because Cuarón decided not to direct the fourth instalment, <i>Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</i>, a new director had to be selected.<sup id="cite_ref-CuaronPotter_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CuaronPotter-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mike_Newell_(director)" title="Mike Newell (director)">Mike Newell</a> was chosen to direct the film, but he declined to direct the next film, <i>Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</i>, which was given to <a href="/wiki/David_Yates" title="David Yates">David Yates</a>, who also directed <i>Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</i> and <i>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</i>, becoming the only director to helm more than one film since Chris Columbus.
</p><p>Chris Columbus said his vision of the first two films was of a "golden storybook, an old-fashioned look", while Alfonso Cuarón changed the visual tone of the series, desaturated the colour palette, and expanded the landscape around <a href="/wiki/Hogwarts" title="Hogwarts">Hogwarts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ColumbusDark_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ColumbusDark-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CuaronPotter_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CuaronPotter-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Mike Newell decided to direct the fourth film as a "paranoid thriller", while David Yates wanted to "bring a sense of jeopardy and character to the world".<sup id="cite_ref-MikeNewellHP_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MikeNewellHP-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DavidYatesEmpire_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DavidYatesEmpire-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Cuarón, Newell, and Yates have said that their challenge was striking a balance between making the films according to their individual vision, while working within a cinematic world already established by Columbus.<sup id="cite_ref-CuaronPotter_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CuaronPotter-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MikeNewellHP_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MikeNewellHP-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DavidYatesEmpire_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DavidYatesEmpire-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>David Heyman commented on the "generosity of the directors" by revealing that "Chris spent time with Alfonso, Alfonso spent time with Mike and Mike spent time with David, showing him an early cut of the film, talking through what it means to be a director and how they went about [making the films]."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>David Heyman also said, "I suppose Chris Columbus was the most conservative choice from the studio's point of view. But he expressed real passion."<sup id="cite_ref-10YearsHP_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10YearsHP-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Producer Tanya Seghatchian said they were "more adventurous" in choosing a director for the third film and went straight to Alfonso Cuarón.<sup id="cite_ref-10YearsHP_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10YearsHP-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Mike Newell became the first British director of the series when he was chosen for the fourth film; Newell was considered to direct the first film before he dropped out.<sup id="cite_ref-10YearsHP_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10YearsHP-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> David Yates directed the final films after David Heyman thought him capable of handling the edgy, emotional, and political material of the later novels.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>All the directors have been supportive of each other. Chris Columbus praised the character development in the films, while Alfonso Cuarón admired the "quiet poetry" of David Yates' films.<sup id="cite_ref-ColumbusDark_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ColumbusDark-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CuaronPotter_39-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CuaronPotter-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Mike Newell noted that each director had a different heroism, and David Yates views the first four films "respectfully and enjoy[s] them."<sup id="cite_ref-MikeNewellHP_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MikeNewellHP-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DavidYatesEmpire_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DavidYatesEmpire-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Daniel Radcliffe said Yates "took the charm of the films that Chris made and the visual flair of everything that Alfonso did and the thoroughly British, bombastic nature of the film directed by Mike Newell" and added "his own sense" of <a href="/wiki/Magic_realism" title="Magic realism">realism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scripts">Scripts</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Steve_Kloves" title="Steve Kloves">Steve Kloves</a> wrote the screenplays for all but the fifth film, which was penned by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Goldenberg" title="Michael Goldenberg">Michael Goldenberg</a>. Kloves had direct assistance from J.K. Rowling, though she allowed him what he described as "tremendous elbow room". Rowling asked Kloves to remain faithful to the spirit of the books; thus, the plot and tone of each film and its corresponding book are virtually the same, albeit with some changes and omissions for purposes of cinematic style, time, and budget constraints. Michael Goldenberg also received input from Rowling during his adaptation of the fifth novel; Goldenberg was originally considered to adapt the first novel before the studio chose Kloves.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hogwarts_model_studio_tour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Hogwarts_model_studio_tour.jpg/220px-Hogwarts_model_studio_tour.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Hogwarts_model_studio_tour.jpg/330px-Hogwarts_model_studio_tour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Hogwarts_model_studio_tour.jpg/440px-Hogwarts_model_studio_tour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hogwarts_model_studio_tour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A studio model of <a href="/wiki/Hogwarts" title="Hogwarts">Hogwarts</a>. It is the main setting in the series; the castle features in every novel and screen adaptation.</div></div></div>
<p>In a 2010 interview, David Heyman briefly explained the book-to-film transition. He commented on Rowling's involvement in the series, stating that she understood that "books and films are different" and was "the best support" a producer could have. Rowling had overall approval on the scripts, which were viewed and discussed by the director and the producers. Heyman also said that Kloves was the "key voice" in the process of adapting the novels and that certain aspects from the books needed to have been excluded from the scripts due to the filmmakers' decision to keep the main focus on Harry's journey as a character, which would ultimately give the films a defined structure. Heyman mentioned that some fans "don't necessarily understand the adaptation process" and that the filmmakers would have loved to "have everything" from the books in the films but noted that it was not possible since they had "neither time nor cinematic structure" to do so. He finished by saying that adapting a novel to the screen is "a really considered process."<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Because the films were being made as the novels were being published, the filmmakers had no idea of the story's outcome until the release of the final novel in 2007. Kloves spoke of his relationship with Rowling when adapting the novels by saying, "The thing is about Jo, which is remarkable for someone who had no experience with the filmmaking process, was her intuition. We had a conversation the very first day I met her where she said, 'I know the movies can't be the books... because I know what's coming and it's impossible to fully dramatise on screen what I'm going to write. But I just ask you to be true to the characters; that's all I care about.'"<sup id="cite_ref-KlovesPotter_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KlovesPotter-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Kloves also said, "I don't know what compelled me to say this [to Rowling], but I said, 'I've just got to warn you my favourite character is not Harry. My favourite character is Hermione.' And I think for some weird reason, from that moment on, she sort of trusted me."<sup id="cite_ref-KlovesPotter_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KlovesPotter-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast_and_crew">Cast and crew</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Harry_Potter_cast_members" title="List of Harry Potter cast members">List of Harry Potter cast members</a></div>
<p>Aside from the three lead actors, other notable cast members include <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Coltrane" title="Robbie Coltrane">Robbie Coltrane</a> as <a href="/wiki/Rubeus_Hagrid" title="Rubeus Hagrid">Rubeus Hagrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Felton" title="Tom Felton">Tom Felton</a> as <a href="/wiki/Draco_Malfoy" title="Draco Malfoy">Draco Malfoy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Rickman" title="Alan Rickman">Alan Rickman</a> as <a href="/wiki/Severus_Snape" title="Severus Snape">Severus Snape</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maggie_Smith" title="Maggie Smith">Dame Maggie Smith</a> as <a href="/wiki/Minerva_McGonagall" class="mw-redirect" title="Minerva McGonagall">Minerva McGonagall</a>. <a href="/wiki/Richard_Harris" title="Richard Harris">Richard Harris</a>, who played the role of Professor <a href="/wiki/Albus_Dumbledore" title="Albus Dumbledore">Albus Dumbledore</a>, died on 25 October 2002 causing the role to be re-cast for the third instalment, <i>Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</i>. David Heyman and director Alfonso Cuarón chose <a href="/wiki/Michael_Gambon" title="Michael Gambon">Michael Gambon</a> to portray the character of Dumbledore, which he did for all succeeding films. Notable recurring cast members include <a href="/wiki/Helena_Bonham_Carter" title="Helena Bonham Carter">Helena Bonham Carter</a> as <a href="/wiki/Bellatrix_Lestrange" class="mw-redirect" title="Bellatrix Lestrange">Bellatrix Lestrange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warwick_Davis" title="Warwick Davis">Warwick Davis</a> as <a href="/wiki/Filius_Flitwick" class="mw-redirect" title="Filius Flitwick">Filius Flitwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Fiennes" title="Ralph Fiennes">Ralph Fiennes</a> as <a href="/wiki/Lord_Voldemort" title="Lord Voldemort">Lord Voldemort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Gleeson" title="Brendan Gleeson">Brendan Gleeson</a> as <a href="/wiki/Alastor_Moody" class="mw-redirect" title="Alastor Moody">Alastor Moody</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Griffiths" title="Richard Griffiths">Richard Griffiths</a> as <a href="/wiki/Vernon_Dursley" class="mw-redirect" title="Vernon Dursley">Vernon Dursley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jason_Isaacs" title="Jason Isaacs">Jason Isaacs</a> as <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Malfoy" class="mw-redirect" title="Lucius Malfoy">Lucius Malfoy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Oldman" title="Gary Oldman">Gary Oldman</a> as <a href="/wiki/Sirius_Black" class="mw-redirect" title="Sirius Black">Sirius Black</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiona_Shaw" title="Fiona Shaw">Fiona Shaw</a> as <a href="/wiki/Petunia_Dursley" class="mw-redirect" title="Petunia Dursley">Petunia Dursley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Spall" title="Timothy Spall">Timothy Spall</a> as <a href="/wiki/Death_Eater#Peter_Pettigrew" title="Death Eater">Peter Pettigrew</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Thewlis" title="David Thewlis">David Thewlis</a> as <a href="/wiki/Remus_Lupin" class="mw-redirect" title="Remus Lupin">Remus Lupin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emma_Thompson" title="Emma Thompson">Emma Thompson</a> as <a href="/wiki/Sybill_Trelawney" class="mw-redirect" title="Sybill Trelawney">Sybill Trelawney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Williams_(actor)" title="Mark Williams (actor)">Mark Williams</a> as <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Weasley" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthur Weasley">Arthur Weasley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Julie_Walters" title="Julie Walters">Julie Walters</a> as <a href="/wiki/Molly_Weasley" class="mw-redirect" title="Molly Weasley">Molly Weasley</a>.
</p><p>The series has seen many returning crew members from various departments, including <a href="/wiki/Tim_Burke_(visual_effects_supervisor)" title="Tim Burke (visual effects supervisor)">Tim Burke</a>, visual effects supervisor; Peter Doyle, digital film colourist; <a href="/wiki/Nick_Dudman" title="Nick Dudman">Nick Dudman</a>, make-up and creature effects designer; <a href="/wiki/David_Holmes_(actor)" title="David Holmes (actor)">David Holmes</a>, stunt double; <a href="/wiki/Amanda_Knight" title="Amanda Knight">Amanda Knight</a>, make-up artist; <a href="/wiki/Stephenie_McMillan" title="Stephenie McMillan">Stephenie McMillan</a>, set designer; <a href="/wiki/Greg_Powell" title="Greg Powell">Greg Powell</a>, stunt coordinator; Jany Temime, costume designer; and <a href="/wiki/Fiona_Weir" title="Fiona Weir">Fiona Weir</a>, casting director.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Set_design">Set design</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hall_of_Christ_Church,_Oxford.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Hall_of_Christ_Church%2C_Oxford.jpg/170px-Hall_of_Christ_Church%2C_Oxford.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Hall_of_Christ_Church%2C_Oxford.jpg/255px-Hall_of_Christ_Church%2C_Oxford.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Hall_of_Christ_Church%2C_Oxford.jpg/340px-Hall_of_Christ_Church%2C_Oxford.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hall_of_Christ_Church,_Oxford.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Hall of <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church,_Oxford" title="Christ Church, Oxford">Christ Church</a> in <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">Oxford</a>, England, the inspiration for the studio film set of The Great Hall of Hogwarts.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The production designer for all eight films is <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Craig" title="Stuart Craig">Stuart Craig</a>. Assisted by <a href="/wiki/Stephenie_McMillan" title="Stephenie McMillan">Stephenie McMillan</a>, Craig has created iconic sets pieces including the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Magic" title="Ministry of Magic">Ministry of Magic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Secrets" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamber of Secrets">Chamber of Secrets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malfoy_Manor" class="mw-redirect" title="Malfoy Manor">Malfoy Manor</a>, and the layout for the CGI <a href="/wiki/Magical_objects_in_Harry_Potter#Horcruxes" title="Magical objects in Harry Potter">Horcrux Cave</a>. Because the novels were being published as the films were being made, Craig was required to rebuild some sets for future films and alter the design of Hogwarts.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Great_Hall,_Hogwarts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/The_Great_Hall%2C_Hogwarts.jpg/220px-The_Great_Hall%2C_Hogwarts.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/The_Great_Hall%2C_Hogwarts.jpg/330px-The_Great_Hall%2C_Hogwarts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/The_Great_Hall%2C_Hogwarts.jpg/440px-The_Great_Hall%2C_Hogwarts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3047" data-file-height="2167" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Great_Hall,_Hogwarts.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The studio film set of The Great Hall of Hogwarts was one of the first sets ever created for the series.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>He said, "In the early days, every time you saw the exterior of Hogwarts, it was a physical miniature," which was made by craftsmen and occupied a large sound stage.<sup id="cite_ref-VanityFairCraig_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VanityFairCraig-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BeatCraig_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BeatCraig-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> "We ended up with a profile of how Hogwarts looked, a skyline that actually I didn't design, and it wasn't always satisfactory, and as all the novels got written and movies got made there were new requirements [for buildings]. The [Astronomy Tower] definitely wasn't there originally, and so we were able to add that substantial piece. And in the last film, we needed an arena for the battle for Hogwarts – the big courtyard outside doubled in size, and if you look at the first movie it wasn't there at all. There were quite some liberties taken with the continuity of Hogwarts."<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In the last film, Craig used a digital model instead of a miniature to "embrace the latest technology".<sup id="cite_ref-BeatCraig_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BeatCraig-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the method of creating the sets, Craig said he often started by sketching ideas onto a blank sheet of paper.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Stephanie McMillan also said that "each film always had plenty of new challenges," citing the changes in visual style between directors and cinematographers as an example, along with the developing story in the novels. Due to J.K. Rowling's descriptions of various settings in the novels, Craig noted his "responsibility was to place it together".<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Craig commented on his experience working in the studio environment: "I'm the production designer, but on a big movie like <i>Harry Potter</i> I may be responsible for 30 to 35 people; from the supervising art director, and a team of art directors and assistants, to draughtsmen and junior draughtsmen, and then on to model makers, sculptors and scenic artists." He said, "Ten years ago, all the <i>Harry Potter</i> drawings were done in pencil. I would take my roughs and plans and sections and give them to a professional architectural illustrator, who would create concept art using pencil and colour wash on watercolour paper." He said the process changed slightly throughout the years due to, what he called, the "digital revolution" of making films.<sup id="cite_ref-BeatCraig_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BeatCraig-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When filming of the series was completed, some of Craig's sets had to be rebuilt or transported for them to be displayed at the Warner Bros. studio tour.<sup id="cite_ref-VanityFairCraig_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VanityFairCraig-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinematography">Cinematography</span></h3>
<p>Six <a href="/wiki/Cinematographer" title="Cinematographer">directors of photography</a> worked on the series: <a href="/wiki/John_Seale" title="John Seale">John Seale</a> on the first film, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Pratt_(cinematographer)" title="Roger Pratt (cinematographer)">Roger Pratt</a> on the second and fourth, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Seresin" title="Michael Seresin">Michael Seresin</a> on the third, <a href="/wiki/S%C5%82awomir_Idziak" title="Sławomir Idziak">Sławomir Idziak</a> on the fifth, <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Delbonnel" title="Bruno Delbonnel">Bruno Delbonnel</a> on the sixth, and <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Serra" title="Eduardo Serra">Eduardo Serra</a> on the seventh and eighth. Delbonnel was considered to return for both parts of <i>Deathly Hallows</i>, but he declined, stating that he was "scared of repeating" himself.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Delbonnel's cinematography in <i>Half-Blood Prince</i> gained the series its only <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nomination for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Cinematography" title="Academy Award for Best Cinematography">Best Cinematography</a>. As the series progressed, each cinematographer faced the challenge of shooting and lighting older sets (which had been around since the first few films) in unique and different ways.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Chris Columbus said the series' vivid colouring decreased as each film was made.<sup id="cite_ref-ColumbusDark_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ColumbusDark-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Michael Seresin commented on the change of visual style from the first two films to <i>Prisoner of Azkaban</i>: "The lighting is moodier, with more shadowing and cross-lighting." Seresin and Alfonso Cuarón moved away from the strongly coloured and brightly lit cinematography of the first two films, with dimmer lighting and a more muted colour palette being utilised for the succeeding five films.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> After comparing a range of digital cameras with 35&#160;mm film, Bruno Delbonnel decided to shoot the sixth movie, <i>Half-Blood Prince</i>, on <a href="/wiki/Film_stock" title="Film stock">film</a> rather than the increasingly popular <a href="/wiki/Digital_cinematography" title="Digital cinematography">digital</a> format. This decision was kept for the two-part <i>Deathly Hallows</i> with Eduardo Serra, who said that he preferred to work with film because it was "more technically accurate and dependable".<sup id="cite_ref-SerraKodak_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SerraKodak-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Because the majority of <i>Deathly Hallows</i> takes place in various settings away from Hogwarts, David Yates wanted to "shake things up" by using different photographic techniques such as using hand-held cameras and very wide camera lenses.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Eduardo Serra said, "Sometimes we are combining elements shot by the main unit, a second unit, and the visual effects unit. You have to know what is being captured – colours, contrast, et cetera – with mathematical precision." He noted that with Stuart Craig's "amazing sets and the story", the filmmakers could not "stray too far from the look of the previous <i>Harry Potter</i> films."<sup id="cite_ref-SerraKodak_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SerraKodak-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Editing">Editing</span></h3>
<p>Along with continuous changes in cinematographers, there have been five <a href="/wiki/Film_editing" title="Film editing">film editors</a> to work in post-production on the series: <a href="/wiki/Richard_Francis-Bruce" title="Richard Francis-Bruce">Richard Francis-Bruce</a> edited the first instalment, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Honess" title="Peter Honess">Peter Honess</a> the second, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Weisberg" title="Steven Weisberg">Steven Weisberg</a> the third, <a href="/wiki/Mick_Audsley" title="Mick Audsley">Mick Audsley</a> the fourth, and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Day_(editor)" title="Mark Day (editor)">Mark Day</a> films five through eight.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Harry_Potter_films" title="Music of the Harry Potter films">Music of the Harry Potter films</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Williams_tux.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/John_Williams_tux.jpg/170px-John_Williams_tux.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/John_Williams_tux.jpg/255px-John_Williams_tux.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/John_Williams_tux.jpg/340px-John_Williams_tux.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Williams_tux.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Williams" title="John Williams">John Williams</a> scored the first three films and received <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Award</a> nominations for the first and third films.</div></div></div>
<p>The <i>Harry Potter</i> series has had four composers. <a href="/wiki/John_Williams" title="John Williams">John Williams</a> scored the first three films: <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone_(soundtrack)" title="Harry Potter and the Philosopher&#39;s Stone (soundtrack)">Philosopher's Stone</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets_(soundtrack)" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets (soundtrack)">Chamber of Secrets</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban_(soundtrack)" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (soundtrack)">Prisoner of Azkaban</a></i>. However, the second entry was adapted and conducted by <a href="/wiki/William_Ross_(composer)" title="William Ross (composer)">William Ross</a> due to Williams's conflicting commitments. Williams also created <i>Hedwig's Theme</i>, which is used in every film in the series.
</p><p>After Williams left the series to pursue other projects, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Doyle" title="Patrick Doyle">Patrick Doyle</a> scored the fourth entry, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire_(soundtrack)" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire (soundtrack)">Goblet of Fire</a></i>, which was directed by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Newell_(director)" title="Mike Newell (director)">Mike Newell</a>, with whom Doyle had worked previously. In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Hooper" title="Nicholas Hooper">Nicholas Hooper</a> started work on the score to <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix_(soundtrack)" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix (soundtrack)">Order of the Phoenix</a></i> by reuniting with director <a href="/wiki/David_Yates" title="David Yates">David Yates</a>. Hooper also composed the soundtrack to <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince_(soundtrack)" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince (soundtrack)">Half-Blood Prince</a></i> but decided not to return for the final films.
</p><p>In January 2010, <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Desplat" title="Alexandre Desplat">Alexandre Desplat</a> was confirmed to compose the score for <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_1_(soundtrack)" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 1 (soundtrack)">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 1</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The film's orchestration started in the summer with <a href="/wiki/Conrad_Pope" title="Conrad Pope">Conrad Pope</a>, the orchestrator on the first three <i>Harry Potter</i> films, collaborating with Desplat. Pope commented that the music "reminds one of the old days."<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Desplat returned to score <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2_(soundtrack)" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2 (soundtrack)">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2</a></i> in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Director David Yates stated that he wanted John Williams to return to the series for the final installment, but their schedules did not align due to the urgent demand for a rough cut of the film.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The final recording sessions of <i>Harry Potter</i> took place on 27 May 2011 at <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road_Studios" title="Abbey Road Studios">Abbey Road Studios</a> with the <a href="/wiki/London_Symphony_Orchestra" title="London Symphony Orchestra">London Symphony Orchestra</a>, orchestrator Conrad Pope, and composer Alexandre Desplat.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Doyle, Hooper, and Desplat introduced their own personal themes to their respective soundtracks, while keeping a few of John Williams's themes.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_effects">Visual effects</span></h3>
<p>There have been many <a href="/wiki/Visual_effects" title="Visual effects">visual effects</a> companies to work on the <i>Harry Potter</i> series. Some of these include <a href="/wiki/Rising_Sun_Pictures" title="Rising Sun Pictures">Rising Sun Pictures</a>, <a href="/wiki/Double_Negative_(VFX)" class="mw-redirect" title="Double Negative (VFX)">Double Negative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cinesite" title="Cinesite">Cinesite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Framestore" title="Framestore">Framestore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic" title="Industrial Light &amp; Magic">Industrial Light &amp; Magic</a>. The latter three have worked on all the films in the series, while Double Negative and Rising Sun Pictures began their commitments with <i>Prisoner of Azkaban</i> and <i>Goblet of Fire</i>, respectively. Framestore contributed by developing many memorable creatures and sequences to the series.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Cinesite was involved in producing both miniature and digital effects for the films.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Producer <a href="/wiki/David_Barron_(film_producer)" title="David Barron (film producer)">David Barron</a> said that "<i>Harry Potter</i> created the UK effects industry as we know it. On the first film, all the complicated visual effects were done on the [US] west coast. But on the second, we took a leap of faith and gave much of what would normally be given to Californian vendors to UK ones. They came up trumps." Tim Burke, the visual effects supervisor, said many studios "are bringing their work to UK effects companies. Every facility is fully booked, and that wasn't the case before <i>Harry Potter</i>. That's really significant."<sup id="cite_ref-10YearsHP_33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10YearsHP-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_filming">Final filming</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Production_of_Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" title="Production of Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows">Production of Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</a></div>
<p>On 12 June 2010, filming of the <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_1" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 1">Deathly Hallows – Part 1</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2">Deathly Hallows – Part 2</a></i> was completed with actor <a href="/wiki/Warwick_Davis" title="Warwick Davis">Warwick Davis</a> stating on his Twitter account, "The end of an Era – today is officially the last day of principal photography on 'Harry Potter' – ever. I feel honoured to be here as the director shouts cut for the very last time. Farewell Harry &amp; Hogwarts, it's been magic!".<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> However, reshoots of the epilogue scene were confirmed to begin in the winter of 2010. The filming was completed on 21 December 2010, marking the official closure of filming the <i>Harry Potter</i> franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Exactly four years earlier on that day, author <a href="/wiki/J._K._Rowling" title="J. K. Rowling">J. K. Rowling</a>'s official website revealed the title of the final novel in the series – <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Films">Films</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HIMG_2604_(8066409156).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/HIMG_2604_%288066409156%29.jpg/220px-HIMG_2604_%288066409156%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/HIMG_2604_%288066409156%29.jpg/330px-HIMG_2604_%288066409156%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/HIMG_2604_%288066409156%29.jpg/440px-HIMG_2604_%288066409156%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HIMG_2604_(8066409156).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Gryffindor Common Room was introduced in the first film.</div></div></div>
<h3><span id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher.27s_Stone_.282001.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher's_Stone_(2001)"><i>Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone</i> (2001)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Philosopher&#39;s Stone (film)">Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone (film)</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Known in India and the United States as <b>Harry Potter and the Sorcerer's Stone</b></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_(character)" title="Harry Potter (character)">Harry Potter</a> is an orphaned boy brought up by his unkind Muggle (non-magical) aunt and uncle. At the age of eleven, half-giant <a href="/wiki/Rubeus_Hagrid" title="Rubeus Hagrid">Rubeus Hagrid</a> informs him that he is actually a <a href="/wiki/Wizard_(fantasy)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wizard (fantasy)">wizard</a> and that his parents were murdered by an evil wizard named <a href="/wiki/Lord_Voldemort" title="Lord Voldemort">Lord Voldemort</a>. Voldemort also attempted to kill one-year-old Harry on the same night, but his killing curse mysteriously rebounded and reduced him to a weak and helpless form. Harry became extremely famous in the <a href="/wiki/Fictional_universe_of_Harry_Potter" title="Fictional universe of Harry Potter">Wizarding World</a> as a result. Harry begins his first year at <a href="/wiki/Hogwarts" title="Hogwarts">Hogwarts School of Witchcraft and Wizardry</a> and learns about magic. During the year, Harry and his friends <a href="/wiki/Ron_Weasley" title="Ron Weasley">Ron Weasley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hermione_Granger" title="Hermione Granger">Hermione Granger</a> become entangled in the mystery of the Philosopher's Stone which is being kept within the school.
</p>
<h3><span id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets_.282002.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets_(2002)"><i>Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets</i> (2002)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Chamber_of_Secrets_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets (film)">Harry Potter and the Chamber of Secrets (film)</a></div>
<p>Harry, Ron, and Hermione return to Hogwarts for their second year, which proves to be more challenging than the last. The <a href="/wiki/Hogwarts#Chamber_of_Secrets" title="Hogwarts">Chamber of Secrets</a> has been opened, leaving students and ghosts petrified by an unleashed monster. Harry must face up to claims that he is the heir of <a href="/wiki/Salazar_Slytherin" class="mw-redirect" title="Salazar Slytherin">Salazar Slytherin</a> (founder of the Chamber), learn that he can speak <a href="/wiki/Parseltongue" class="mw-redirect" title="Parseltongue">Parseltongue</a>, and also discover the properties of a mysterious diary, only to find himself trapped within the Chamber of Secrets itself.
</p>
<h3><span id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban_.282004.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban_(2004)"><i>Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</i> (2004)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (film)">Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (film)</a></div>
<p>Harry Potter's third year sees the boy wizard, along with his friends, attending Hogwarts School once again. <a href="/wiki/Remus_Lupin" class="mw-redirect" title="Remus Lupin">Professor R. J. Lupin</a> joins the staff as Defence Against the Dark Arts teacher, while convicted murderer <a href="/wiki/Sirius_Black" class="mw-redirect" title="Sirius Black">Sirius Black</a> escapes from <a href="/wiki/Azkaban" class="mw-redirect" title="Azkaban">Azkaban Prison</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Magic" title="Ministry of Magic">Ministry of Magic</a> entrusts the <a href="/wiki/Dementor" class="mw-redirect" title="Dementor">Dementors of Azkaban</a> to guard Hogwarts from Black. Harry learns more about his past and his connection with the escaped prisoner.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HIMG_2738_(8066424073).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/HIMG_2738_%288066424073%29.jpg/220px-HIMG_2738_%288066424073%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/HIMG_2738_%288066424073%29.jpg/330px-HIMG_2738_%288066424073%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/HIMG_2738_%288066424073%29.jpg/440px-HIMG_2738_%288066424073%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HIMG_2738_(8066424073).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Riddles' Gravestone from Lord Voldemort's rebirth scene in the fourth film.</div></div></div>
<h3><span id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire_.282005.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire_(2005)"><i>Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</i> (2005)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire (film)">Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire (film)</a></div>
<p>During Harry's fourth year, Hogwarts plays host to a legendary event: the <a href="/wiki/Triwizard_Tournament" class="mw-redirect" title="Triwizard Tournament">Triwizard Tournament</a>. Three European schools participate in the tournament, with three 'champions' representing each school in the deadly tasks. The <a href="/wiki/Goblet_of_Fire" class="mw-redirect" title="Goblet of Fire">Goblet of Fire</a> chooses <a href="/wiki/Fleur_Delacour" class="mw-redirect" title="Fleur Delacour">Fleur Delacour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Krum" class="mw-redirect" title="Viktor Krum">Viktor Krum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cedric_Diggory" class="mw-redirect" title="Cedric Diggory">Cedric Diggory</a> to compete against each other. However, curiously, Harry's name is also produced from the Goblet thus making him a fourth champion, which results in a terrifying encounter with a reborn Lord Voldemort.
</p>
<h3><span id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix_.282007.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix_(2007)"><i>Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</i> (2007)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix (film)">Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix (film)</a></div>
<p>Harry's fifth year begins with him being attacked by Dementors in Little Whinging. Later, he finds out that the Ministry of Magic is in denial of Lord Voldemort's return. Harry is also beset by disturbing and realistic nightmares, while Professor <a href="/wiki/Dolores_Umbridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Dolores Umbridge">Umbridge</a>, a representative of Minister for Magic <a href="/wiki/Cornelius_Fudge" class="mw-redirect" title="Cornelius Fudge">Cornelius Fudge</a>, is the new Defence Against the Dark Arts teacher. Harry becomes aware that Voldemort is after a prophecy which reveals: "neither can live while the other survives". The rebellion involving the students of Hogwarts, secret organisation <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Phoenix_(fiction)" class="mw-redirect" title="Order of the Phoenix (fiction)">Order of the Phoenix</a>, the Ministry of Magic, and the Death Eaters begins.
</p>
<h3><span id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince_.282009.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince_(2009)"><i>Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</i> (2009)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince (film)">Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince (film)</a></div>
<p>In Harry's sixth year at Hogwarts, Lord Voldemort and his Death Eaters are increasing their terror upon the Wizarding and <a href="/wiki/Muggle" title="Muggle">Muggle</a> worlds. Headmaster <a href="/wiki/Albus_Dumbledore" title="Albus Dumbledore">Albus Dumbledore</a> persuades his old friend <a href="/wiki/Horace_Slughorn" class="mw-redirect" title="Horace Slughorn">Horace Slughorn</a> to return to Hogwarts as a professor as there is a vacancy to fill. There is a more important reason, however, for Slughorn's return. While in a Potions lesson, Harry takes possession of a strangely annotated school textbook, inscribed 'This is the property of the Half-Blood Prince'. <a href="/wiki/Draco_Malfoy" title="Draco Malfoy">Draco Malfoy</a> struggles to carry out a deed presented to him by Voldemort. Meanwhile, Dumbledore and Harry secretly work together to discover the method on how to destroy the Dark Lord once and for all.
</p>
<h3><span id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_.E2.80.93_Part_1_.282010.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_–_Part_1_(2010)"><i>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 1</i> (2010)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_1" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 1">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 1</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Potter%27s_cottage,_Godric%27s_Hollow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Potter%27s_cottage%2C_Godric%27s_Hollow.jpg/220px-Potter%27s_cottage%2C_Godric%27s_Hollow.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Potter%27s_cottage%2C_Godric%27s_Hollow.jpg/330px-Potter%27s_cottage%2C_Godric%27s_Hollow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Potter%27s_cottage%2C_Godric%27s_Hollow.jpg/440px-Potter%27s_cottage%2C_Godric%27s_Hollow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3047" data-file-height="2295" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Potter%27s_cottage,_Godric%27s_Hollow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Potters' Cottage from the final film</div></div></div>
<p>After unexpected events at the end of the previous year, Harry, Ron, and Hermione are entrusted with a quest to find and destroy Lord Voldemort's secret to immortality – the <a href="/wiki/Horcrux" class="mw-redirect" title="Horcrux">Horcruxes</a>. It is supposed to be their final year at Hogwarts, but the collapse of the Ministry of Magic and Voldemort's rise to power prevents them from attending. The trio undergo a long journey with many obstacles in their path including Death Eaters, Snatchers, the mysterious <a href="/wiki/Deathly_Hallows_(object)" class="mw-redirect" title="Deathly Hallows (object)">Deathly Hallows</a>, and Harry's connection with the Dark Lord's mind becoming ever stronger.
</p>
<h3><span id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_.E2.80.93_Part_2_.282011.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_–_Part_2_(2011)"><i>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2</i> (2011)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2</a></div>
<p>After destroying one Horcrux and discovering the significance of the three Deathly Hallows, Harry, Ron and Hermione continue to seek the other Horcruxes in an attempt to destroy Voldemort, who has now obtained the powerful <a href="/wiki/Elder_Wand" class="mw-redirect" title="Elder Wand">Elder Wand</a>. The Dark Lord discovers Harry's hunt for Horcruxes and launches an attack on Hogwarts School, where the trio return for one last stand against the dark forces that threaten the Wizarding and Muggle worlds.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span></h2>
<p>The rights for the first four novels in the series were sold to Warner Bros. for £1,000,000 by J.K. Rowling. After the release of the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Goblet_of_Fire" title="Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire">fourth book</a> in July 2000, the first film, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Philosopher&#39;s Stone (film)">Harry Potter and the Philosopher's Stone</a></i>, was released on 16 November 2001. In its opening weekend, the film grossed $90 million in the United States alone, which set a record opening worldwide. The succeeding three motion picture adaptations followed suit in financial success, while garnering positive reviews from fans and critics. The fifth film, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix (film)">Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</a></i>, was released by Warner Bros. on 11 July 2007 in English-speaking countries, except for the UK and Ireland, which released the movie on 12 July.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The sixth, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince (film)">Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</a></i>, was released on 15 July 2009 to critical acclaim and finished its theatrical run ranked as the number two grossing <a href="/wiki/2009_in_film" title="2009 in film">film of 2009</a> on the worldwide charts.
</p><p>The final novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</a></i>, was split into two cinematic parts: <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_-_Part_1" class="mw-redirect" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows - Part 1"><i>Part 1</i></a> was released on 19 November 2010, and <a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_-_Part_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows - Part 2"><i>Part 2</i></a>, the conclusion to both the final film and the series, was released on 15 July 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-final-three-potter-films_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-final-three-potter-films-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> <i>Part 1</i> was originally scheduled to be released in <a href="/wiki/3-D_film" class="mw-redirect" title="3-D film">3D</a> and 2D,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> but due to a delay in the 3D conversion process, Warner Bros. released the film only in 2D and IMAX cinemas. However, <i>Part 2</i> was released in 2D and 3D cinemas as originally planned.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The television broadcast rights for the series in the United States are currently held by <a href="/wiki/NBCUniversal" title="NBCUniversal">NBCUniversal</a>, which typically airs the films on <a href="/wiki/USA_Network" title="USA Network">USA Network</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syfy" title="Syfy">Syfy</a>. <sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The film series has accrued nearly 1.3 billion viewings since its television debut—the highest-watched franchise in television broadcast history.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response">Critical response</span></h3>
<p>All the films have been a success financially and critically, making the franchise one of the major Hollywood "tent-poles" akin to <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_(film_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="James Bond (film series)">James Bond</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Indiana_Jones_(franchise)" title="Indiana Jones (franchise)">Indiana Jones</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean_(film_series)" title="Pirates of the Caribbean (film series)">Pirates of the Caribbean</a></i>. The series is noted by audiences for growing visually <a href="/wiki/Dark_fantasy" title="Dark fantasy">darker</a> and more mature as each film was released.<sup id="cite_ref-ColumbusDark_34-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ColumbusDark-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> However, opinions of the films generally divide book fans, with some preferring the more faithful approach of the first two films and others preferring the more stylised character-driven approach of the later films.
</p><p>Some also feel the series has a "disjointed" feel due to the changes in directors, as well as Michael Gambon's interpretation of Albus Dumbledore differing from that of Richard Harris. Author <a href="/wiki/J._K._Rowling" title="J. K. Rowling">J. K. Rowling</a> has been constantly supportive of the films,<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> and evaluated <i>Deathly Hallows</i> as her favourite one in the series. She wrote on her website of the changes in the book-to-film transition, "It is simply impossible to incorporate every one of my storylines into a film that has to be kept under four hours long. Obviously films have restrictions – novels do not have constraints of time and budget; I can create dazzling effects relying on nothing but the interaction of my own and my readers' imaginations".<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span></h3>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/64th_British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="64th British Academy Film Awards">64th British Academy Film Awards</a> in February 2011, <a href="/wiki/J._K._Rowling" title="J. K. Rowling">J. K. Rowling</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Heyman" title="David Heyman">David Heyman</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Barron_(film_producer)" title="David Barron (film producer)">David Barron</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Yates" title="David Yates">David Yates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso Cuarón">Alfonso Cuarón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Newell_(director)" title="Mike Newell (director)">Mike Newell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Grint" title="Rupert Grint">Rupert Grint</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emma_Watson" title="Emma Watson">Emma Watson</a> collected the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Outstanding_British_Contribution_to_Cinema_Award" title="BAFTA Outstanding British Contribution to Cinema Award">Michael Balcon Award for Outstanding British Contribution to Cinema</a> for the series.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition, the <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">American Film Institute</a> recognised the entire series with a Special Award at the <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute_Awards_2011" title="American Film Institute Awards 2011">American Film Institute Awards</a> in 2011. Special awards "are given to outstanding achievements in the moving image that do not fit into AFI's criteria for the other honorees." <sup id="cite_ref-afi.com_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afi.com-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> In its press release, the Institute referred to the films as "a landmark series; eight films that earned the trust of a generation who wished for the beloved books of J.K. Rowling to come to life on the silver screen. The collective wizardry of an epic ensemble gave us the gift of growing older with Harry, Ron and Hermione as the magic of Hogwarts sprung from the films and into the hearts and minds of Muggles around the world." <sup id="cite_ref-afi.com_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afi.com-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Harry Potter</i> was also recognised by the <a href="/wiki/Britannia_Awards" title="Britannia Awards">BAFTA Los Angeles Britannia Awards</a>, with David Yates winning the Britannia Award for Artistic Excellence in Directing for his four <i>Harry Potter</i> films.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Six of the eight films were nominated for a total of 12 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a>.
</p><p>Some critics, fans, and general audiences have expressed disappointment that the <i>Harry Potter</i> series did not win any Oscars for its achievements. However, others have pointed out that certain films in the series had uneven reviews, in contrast to the three films of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)" title="The Lord of the Rings (film series)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i>, for example, which were all critically acclaimed. This has been partially attributed to the <i>Harry Potter</i> franchise going through several directors with their own styles in contrast to the <i>Lord of the Rings</i> trilogy, which was filmed in one massive undertaking by the same director, writer, and producer.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although not successful at the Oscars, the <i>Harry Potter</i> series has gained success in many other award ceremonies, including the annual <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award" title="Saturn Award">Saturn Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Art_Directors_Guild" title="Art Directors Guild">Art Directors Guild Awards</a>. The series has also gained a total of 24 nominations at the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="British Academy Film Awards">British Academy Film Awards</a> presented at the annual <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">BAFTAs</a>, winning several, and 5 nominations at the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harry_Potter_cast.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Harry_Potter_cast.jpg/220px-Harry_Potter_cast.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Harry_Potter_cast.jpg/330px-Harry_Potter_cast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Harry_Potter_cast.jpg/440px-Harry_Potter_cast.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harry_Potter_cast.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Radcliffe, Grint, and Watson were honored outside <a href="/wiki/Grauman%27s_Chinese_Theatre" title="Grauman&#39;s Chinese Theatre">Grauman's Chinese Theatre</a> at the Hand, Foot, and Wand Ceremony, <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>, July 2007.</div></div></div>
<p><i>Philosopher's Stone</i> achieved seven BAFTA Award nominations, including Best British Film and Best Supporting Actor for <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Coltrane" title="Robbie Coltrane">Robbie Coltrane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bafta_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bafta-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The film was also nominated for eight Saturn Awards and won for its costumes design.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> It was also nominated at the <a href="/wiki/Art_Directors_Guild" title="Art Directors Guild">Art Directors Guild Awards</a> for its production design<sup id="cite_ref-adg_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adg-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> and received the <a href="/wiki/7th_Critics%27_Choice_Awards" title="7th Critics&#39; Choice Awards">Broadcast Film Critics Award</a> for Best Live Action Family Film along with gaining two other nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-bfca_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bfca-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Chamber of Secrets</i> won the award for Best Live Action Family Film in the Phoenix Film Critics Society. It was nominated for seven Saturn Awards, including Best Director and Best Fantasy Film. The film was nominated for four BAFTA Awards and a Grammy Award for John Williams's score. <i>Prisoner of Azkaban</i> won an Audience Award, as well as Best Feature Film, at the BAFTA Awards. The film also won a BMI Film Music award along with being nominated at the Grammy Awards, Visual Effect Society Awards, and the Amanda Awards. <i>Goblet of Fire</i> won a BAFTA award for <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Production_Design" title="BAFTA Award for Best Production Design">Best Production Design</a> as well as being nominated at the Saturn Awards, Critic's Choice Awards, and the Visual Effects Society Awards.
</p><p><i>Order of the Phoenix</i> picked up three awards at the inaugural <a href="/wiki/ITV_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="ITV Network">ITV</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Movie_Awards" title="National Movie Awards">National Movie Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Empire_Awards" title="Empire Awards">Empire Awards</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Yates" title="David Yates">David Yates</a> won Best Director.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Composer <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Hooper" title="Nicholas Hooper">Nicholas Hooper</a> received a nomination for a World Soundtrack Discovery Award.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The film was nominated at the BAFTA Awards, but did not win for Best Production Design or Best Special Visual Effects.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> <i>Half-Blood Prince</i> was nominated for BAFTA Awards in Production Design and Visual Effects,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> and it was in the longlists for several other categories, including Best Supporting Actor for <a href="/wiki/Alan_Rickman" title="Alan Rickman">Alan Rickman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Amongst other nominations and wins, the film also achieved Best Family Movie at the <a href="/wiki/National_Movie_Awards" title="National Movie Awards">National Movie Awards</a> as well as Best Live Action Family Film at the Phoenix Film Critics Society Awards, along with being nominated for Best Motion Picture at the <a href="/wiki/Satellite_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Satellite Award">Satellite Awards</a>.
</p><p><i>Deathly Hallows – Part 1</i> gained two nominations at the BAFTA Awards for Best Make-Up and Hair and Best Visual Effects, along with receiving nominations for the same categories at the Broadcast Film Critics Association Awards. <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Serra" title="Eduardo Serra">Eduardo Serra</a>'s cinematography and <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Craig" title="Stuart Craig">Stuart Craig</a>'s production design were also nominated in various award ceremonies, and David Yates attained his second win at the Empire Awards, this time for Best Fantasy Film. He also obtained another Best Director nomination at the annual Saturn Awards, which also saw the film gain a Best Fantasy Film nomination.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> <i>Deathly Hallows – Part 2</i> was released to critical acclaim, gaining a mix of audience awards. Part 2 of <i>Deathly Hallows</i> was also recognised at the Saturn Awards as well as the BAFTA Awards, where the film achieved a win for <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Special_Visual_Effects" title="BAFTA Award for Best Special Visual Effects">Best Special Visual Effects</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office_performance">Box office performance</span></h3>
<p>As of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Harry_Potter_(film_series)&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the <i>Harry Potter</i> film series is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_film_series#Highest-grossing_franchises_and_film_series" class="mw-redirect" title="List of highest-grossing film series">3rd highest-grossing film franchise</a> of all time, with the eight films released grossing over $7.7&#160;billion worldwide. Without adjusting for inflation, this is higher than the first 22 <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_(film_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="James Bond (film series)">James Bond</a></i> films and the six films in the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chris_Columbus_(filmmaker)" title="Chris Columbus (filmmaker)">Chris Columbus</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Philosopher%27s_Stone_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Philosopher&#39;s Stone (film)">Philosopher's Stone</a></i> became the highest-grossing <i>Harry Potter</i> film worldwide upon completing its theatrical run in 2002, but it was eventually topped by <a href="/wiki/David_Yates" title="David Yates">David Yates</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2">Deathly Hallows – Part 2</a></i>, while <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_Cuar%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso Cuarón">Alfonso Cuarón</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Prisoner_of_Azkaban_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban (film)">Prisoner of Azkaban</a></i> grossed the least.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Six films in the <i>Harry Potter</i> franchise — <i>Harry Potter and the Prisoner of Azkaban</i>, <i>Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire</i>, <i>Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</i>, <i>Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</i> and <i>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</i>, Parts 1 &amp; 2 — have to date grossed around $216 million in <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> theaters worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
